<Rate>2<//Rate>< Review>
Back in july i took our frenchie there because he had severe diarrhea and ended up staying there for 5 days. He had no other symptoms so my first thought is salmonella since he did eat cooked chicken before. Turns out he had nothing wrong, no infection nor bacteria ( which made no sense). At pick up i was given antibiotics incase he did have something and that seemed to have been working for him there i guess ( still not making sense). So on my way to the car he coughs and im like "okay" this better not be kennel cough because he didn't have it before". I get home and he's coughing more and i wait a day or two before i call the clinic to make sure it's not a dry throat. They prescribe clavamox and temaril over the phone. So im thinking ok this should work since it just started. I notice neither meds is working but i wait to finish the temaril since it helps open the airways. Let me say i have always worked as a vet tech since i was 17 and stopped about 5-6 yrs ago cuz i had to raise my son. And i know if the meds aren't working its because its beyond just a cough now. I take him back and i tell them i recieved him back sicker, turns out it was a respiratory infection almost turning into broncolitis. Both lungs and heart were inflamed. I was upset because kennel cough is the cause for this and kennel cough is airborne. Meaning the dog who had it wasn't isolated from other dogs or the clinic lacks in sanitizing the exam rooms. I mentioned it to the doc and was given a discount. And to top it off his cough lasted 2 months.
This shouldn't have gone unnoticed, when you are in treatment medicating and observing the pets that stay over night your job is to mention it on the file but it wasn't. This is very irresponsible that means this place isn't being run correctly. Every vet i have ever worked at has one big rule which is " always clean the exam room before and after" and sanitize the floors often and that's something colima does not do. My heart sanked because i know breeders who have gone to colima and had their pups died from a bad respiratory infection.  But we had not experienced it yet up until that day. I understand you techs at colima are busy but a way to make it easier and smoother for everyone is to do what's easy first.
Vaccines, deworming, and progesterone test should be seen first. You don't need to take them to the back or to a room, it can be done in the car or up front. Medication, drop off and pick up can be done by two or 3 girls. And last should be the dogs waiting for an exam. This way things are out of the way and so are people.< /Review>

Unless you're a bully breeder, I would go elsewhere.< /Text>

<Date>1598080579576</Date><text>Brought my French Bulldog, Yoda, to have her babies here. One week before Yoda‚Äôs due date, we had her complete an X-ray for puppy size and puppy count. A week later we noticed Yoda experiencing some contractions, we drove to Colima Animal Hospital. I could not be happier with the service. Vet had a reverse progesterone test completed. The results did take approximately 2 hours so we did wait quite some time. However, after receiving the results vet decided it was a good time for Yoda to deliver the pups. The whole experience did remind me of when having my own children. Lol After a 6-7 hour wait, Mommy came out very strong from delivering her babies and the litter of 6 pups was very healthy as well. It was a long wait, but worth it!!!! Seems a bit chaotic at first, but after all is said and done I could not be any happier. Mommy and babies would agree as well. The litter is now 7 weeks old and I have to admit Colima Animal Hospital staff was very helpful and supportive every step of the way. She uncompassionatly yanked my puppy away from me so hard over the wide counter they have there, that when she handed him back to me he was coughing and very scared and frightened, so much so that we saw the vet that was available to make sure he was alright. We even had to call the front desk while we were sitting there because they forgot us and took so long just to get us in to see the vet.
When we asked for any copies of the paper and receipts she responded condescendingly, and very slowly got the paperwork after being asked four times for it and after we telephoned the desk again.
When we finally did get the paperwork telling us what shots were done we realized she did not do what I asked for.I told her exactly what shot I needed for my puppy three times and I even wrote it down for her and instead she gave him a different shot, not the one I asked for at all. She didn't even bother to say that they didn't have the shot I needed even though she had the chance to and when I asked if they had the shot I needed she even said yes, that they had it.
When we got him home he yelped whenever we touched his chest. It was not because of his shot, because the shot was on his shoulder, not his chest. It got bad enough that we took him back to the Colima Animal Hospital to have him looked at and x-rayed, there were no breaks or broken ribs. His chest area is probably bruised from Maddy grabbing him and picking him up so roughly and uncaringly, in a way that did not support his body at all.
He is still yelping and coughing when his chest is touched. He was even checked for kennel cough so that is not the issue. We had to take him to another vet today and pay another vet fee to make sure he is truly alright.
Maddy is ill-fit, uncompassionate, lacks hospitality, condescending, deaf, hateful, and obviously cannot read, and lacks knowledge of her job. She does not deserve to be in the position that she is in, and she makes Colima Animal Hospital look very bad, which is a shame because the vets are very kind. I'm embarrassed for them.
I'm only giving them one star because the veterinarians and the other office staff are nice, but even with that being said this is how bad Maddy makes them look, she is a liability for Colima Animal Hospital.

< review>
First impression coming into this office it was clean, love the decor and the staff was extremely friendly and attentive as soon as you walk in the door. Not like a regular snooty dermatologist office where they don't pay any attention to you and make you a bit intimidated for even going. That set the tone for the entire visit.

After getting a consultation and a plan from Dr. Newman; who is highly knowledgeable in everything dermatology and more. He immediately made me feel comfortable and listened to what I wanted.

Nurse Danielle gave me my first treatment today and although I felt a bit embarrassed of my skin; I've never actually been one to go to a dermatologist or even get a facial and I'm 35! She made me throw my worries way and made the appointment a breeze. She was professional, friendly and well versed in all of the treatments that they recommended. She was able to answer all of my questions, refreshing how knowledgeable she was. The lasers and peels targeted my skin issues... I scar or get brown spots easily and I had a few pimple like cysts that she was able to take care of. I can't wait to continue going there (even though the drive is 1.5 hrs for me coming from OC - it shows that it's worth it!).

Thank you Dr. Newman, Nurse Danielle and the team for making my first visit an amazing one. Can't wait to see the results and feel more confident in my skin.<//review>

< Name>
Joseph Fisher< /Name>
< Date>
1536207341357</Date>
<rating>5<//rating>< review>
I've been on this tour 3 times now, and it's my go-to thing to do when I have out of town friends come visit the Bay Area. The views are spectacular! You get to see the Golden Gate Bridge, Bay Bridge, AT&T Park, and many other great sights from a unique perspective that very few actually get to see. You get to geek out in fowl weather gear, and hop out into the Pacific Ocean in a super fast and super fun boat. But the thing that really makes this tour great is the guide - Captain Charles. He's extremely personable, knowledgable, and always has an enthusiastic attitude. Clearly Captain Charles loves it when his passengers have an outstanding time out on the Bay. He's 3 for 3 with me, and I expect many more trips in the future.

The Bay Voyager rib boat surprisingly makes for a smooth ride, despite being insanely fast & seemingly lightweight. It's great fun racing out to the Golden Gate Bridge and beyond, but Captain Charles is mindful of who's on board, and I've seen him tailor the speed to those who may appreciate a more gentle trip. He regularly checks in to make sure everybody is having fun, and I've seen him speed up and slow down based on how people are experiencing the ride. He's very attentive to who's on board, and does a great job of customizing the game plan on the fly.

The commentary is fantastic. You learn about the history of the early 1900s earthquake and subsequent fire, as well as history around a merchant ship that was involved in the Normandy armada in WW2, along with a sub that never missed a torpedo hit. Captain Charles actually served on the crew of the WW2 ship in a reunion event - great stories there! You also get to see lighthouses, hiking trails, extremely overpriced housing (hey it is the Bay Area), World's Fair monuments, Lucas Arts studios, and a gazillion other San Francisco shoreline sights. Most locals will spend decades here before seeing most of what you'll see on this tour.

I first found Bay Voyager after taking an out of town friend on a visit to Alcatraz, and we both found the boat ride to be way more fun than the island itself. On subsequent visits, I've found everybody absolutely loves this tour. Everybody likes Dolores Park, Twin Peaks, and a Giants game, but they all rave about zipping across the bay on Bay Voyager!

This is absolutely a must-do if you're visiting the Bay Area. You'll have a blast.<//review>

We felt very safe at all times during our adventure. We wore rain slicker gear he provided and the provided life jackets, so we were warm and dry the entire trip. A life-long Bay area resident, Captain Charles brings forward a much different telling of the sanitized historical fiction that is that unconsciously told by other tour operaters on the waterfront. <name>Sneha Patel</name>< Date>
1497299020863<//Date>
< rate>
5< /rate>
<Text>What an amazing way to spend a Saturday morning! We did the early bird trip on Bay Voyager and my 7 year old son talked of nothing else all weekend long. We are Bay Area residents and have done all the usual things: numerous trips to Alcatraz, taking the ferry between Oakland and SF, dinner cruises around the Bay, etc.  This was by far the best of the lot: the most exciting and the most fun! It was really different too, being in a smaller boat (they operate the same rigid-bottomed dinghies that are used by the coastguard and the navy) and feeling the waves under us as we rode out at high speed towards the Golden Gate Bridge, under the bridge and into the Pacific. We saw the San Francisco shoreline all the way around to China Beach and Land's End. Every now and then, the boat would stop and Captain Charles Jennings, who owns and operates Bay Voyager, would regale us with historical facts about the sights in front of us or some fascinating local lore. It was clear to us that he's a born native of the Bay Area who loves it deeply and knows it intimately. My favorite part of the trip (and that if my kids) was going under the bridge, and seeing it up close. When we circled back around, Captain Charles and Captain Brian took us in to where the sea lions where lying on their wooden flats, much to the envy of the onlookers lined up along the decks on Pier 39! Because of the size of the boat, we were able to see them at close range, particularly great for the kids! I liked the fact that they went in really slowly and quietly so as not to disturb the sea lions or scare the many sea lion pups we saw.

From the very beginning (the welcome, being outfitted with waterproof gear and getting our life jackets on) to the very end (disembarking and being bid farewell), it was such a lovely experience. The boat is very clean and the seats are comfortably cushioned. Captain Charles is gracious, considerate, experienced, great with kids (turns out he has a 5 year old son so he really relates well and understands how to put the kids at their ease) and has an excellent sense of humor. I would recommend this trip to locals like us, or tourists! We will have friends visiting us from Europe in the Fall and I'm going to book all of us on the longer afternoon ride. I know they and their two kids will love it, and we will be happy to do it with them!

I should mention that I forgot my cell phone in the pocket of the waterproof jacket that I was wearing. By the time I realized this and rushed back to the dock, Captain Charles and Captain Brian had put most of the jackets away in the locker. They very kindly took each one out and checked the pockets until they found my cell phone. I felt awful about putting them to so much trouble but they were super nice about it! Also, they take photos of you in the boat and you don't have to pay anything extra for these- really nice when you consider how much you get nickeled and dimed for every extra thing on some other rides.

TIP: DO wear layers! And even if it's a gorgeous sunny San Francisco morning, which it was when we went out yesterday, wear a hat or tie back your hair as the wind will rush by as the boat gathers speed. The hat or woolly head band will also keep your ears warm in the wind. And sun glasses are a MUST; we were all glad we'd taken ours. If the kids don't have any, they do have sets for them.

NOTE: My kids both loved this, and they are young! Bay Voyager takes safety very seriously and gives clear instructions. Kids do have to be 5 and older, though.< /Text>< pictures>
None< /pictures>

<gmapID>0x80952f9ea08e834f:0x27de00be193d55<//gmapID>< Text>
Service is courteous and prompt. If you're coming in around 1030 to 11 am it will be busy so expect a 15 minute wait for food. The eggs were standard for a cafe slightly fluffy but also dry. The eggs could use a little butter or creme fresh nearing the end of cooking to be knockout food. The bacon was crisp and was oven cooked and into the fryer. You can taste a little bit of the frying oil. I also sampled a 1/2 waffle, it was excellent and it paired with the syrup wonderfully. The waffle was fluffy, absorbent, and had a flavor of vanilla to it. Expect to pay 10 to 14 dollars a plaque for a plate. The coffee was 2.75.  They do offer "cappuccino" which is a flavor mix. Overall if I had extra money and wanted to go out for breakfast, I would definitely come back.</Text>

I have been a fan of the home made sausage patties for almost 5 years.
Although ---
The recipe ALMOST SEEMS to be the same, except it's missing those key little ingredients that use to set it apart from the rest. The patty I was served was  a little dry,  thin and flat instead of thick & juicy with visible "seeds & spices" .
The original taste and Quality has gone down and
Their prices have gone up since they moved over to this new location.
Average cost of a basic plate for breakfast , a
The License Plate Wall is how my kids know this place. It is big, clean and just a really nice comfortable atmosphere unless you sit at the diner style counter.
There's alot of movement and noise due to the waitresses picking up their orders.
So it's not the best place to sit if your reading something. Another thing that has changed is the biscuits and gravey.
Biscuits are NOT HOMEMADE anymore.
Salsa has changed and tastes like a glop of squished can tomatoes.</review>

< text>
I always watch to see which restraunts contractors, farmers, and blue collar families frequent. And the Corner Cafe is one of these gems. Great Food, Great Service, Great Prices. The restraunt is open for breakfast and lunch. Bring your appetite, and try the Meat Loaf special on Wednesday's. The location can be hard to recognize your first time. As you head North on Akers, past the National Guard Armory the restraunt is on the side of the shopping center facing Akers. Parking is tight, and you may need to park a little ways from the restraunt.< /text>
